The court also affirmed the trial court's order requiring defendant to pay monies that were incorrectly assessed against plaintiff into an account for plaintiff and to pay plaintiff's counsel fees. Finally, the court reversed the trial court's finding that the Act had been violated because board members were not made parties to the suit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the trial court' s judgment which held that defendant's local amusement tax had not violated plaintiff amusement entity's constitutional rights to due process, but had violated plaintiff's constitutional rights to equal protection. The court reversed the trial court's finding against defendant for an alleged violation of local tax laws because necessary officials were not made parties to the suit.

Professional Ins. Agents Ass'n v. Chronister


No. 696 C. D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


155 Pa. Commw. 652; 625 A.2d 1314; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 324


December 16, 1992, Argued  
May 25, 1993, Decided  
May 25, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. FC90-01. State Agency, Insurance Commissioner of PA



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the February 27, 1992 order of the Insurance Commissioner is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an association of professional insurance agents and a licensed Pennsylvania insurance agent, sought review of an order from respondent Pennsylvania Insurance Commissioner, which dismissed a part of petitioners' formal complaint in which they challenged certain rules found in the Pennsylvania Assigned Risk Plan, established under § 1741 of the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1741.


OVERVIEW: Respondent Pennsylvania Insurance Commissioner dismissed part of a complaint filed by petitioners, a group of professional insurance agents and a licensed agent, challenging the "take-out provision" of the Pennsylvania Assigned Risk Plan, an unincorporated association governed by insurance representatives that insured high risk drivers. Petitioners sought review, claiming various bases for invalidation of the plan, including unconstitutionality. The court affirmed. The court held that the take-out provision was not unconstitutional under federal or state law because it did not involve state action. The court sustained respondent's finding of an insufficient nexus between the plan and the commonwealth and held that the commonwealth's pervasive regulation of the plan did not make the plan's actions into "state actions." The cooperation between the commonwealth and the plan, the alleged "adoption" of the plan by the Department of Insurance, and the approval of the plan by respondent were insufficient grounds for finding that the plan was a state actor whose conduct had to comport with constitutional requirements.


OUTCOME: The court upheld a ruling by respondent Pennsylvania Insurance Commissioner dismissing part of a complaint filed by petitioners, a group of professional insurance agents and a licensed agent, which challenged the "take-out provision" of the Pennsylvania Assigned Risk Plan. The nexus between the plan and the commonwealth was insufficient to support a finding that the plan was a state actor for constitutional purposes.

Brown v. Commonwealth


No. 331 M. D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


155 Pa. Commw. 197; 624 A.2d 795; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 249


December 17, 1992, Argued  
April 22, 1993, Decided  
April 22, 1993, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Respondents' preliminary objection in the form of a demurrer shall be sustained, and Petitioners' Petition for Review is dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Before the court (Pennsylvania) in its original jurisdiction were the preliminary objections of respondent Commonwealth to the request for review by petitioner, professional lobbyists and organizations that purchase lobbying services. Petitioners filed an action asking the court to declare a section of the tax code unconstitutional as applied to them and to enjoin its enforcement.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, professional lobbyists and organizations that purchase lobbying services, contended, among other things, that imposing the 6% sales tax on lobbying services was unconstitutional because lobbying was a protected form of speech under the U.S. Const. amend. V and XIV, and that the sales tax on lobbying would infringe on the exercise of that speech by inhibiting petitioners' right to petition the government for redress of grievances. The court rejected petitioners' contentions. The court held that a non-content based sales tax that did not single out particular speakers did not violate the free speech rights protected under the United States or Pennsylvania Constitutions. The court held that petitioners failed to state a claim, under the U.S. Const. amend. I and XIV, for which relief could be granted. The court also held that petitioners failed to state a cause of action under the U.S. Const. amend. I, and Pa. Const. art. I, § 7. Accordingly, the court sustained respondent Commonwealth's preliminary objection in the form of a demurrer, and dismissed the petition for review.


OUTCOME: The court sustained respondent Commonwealths' preliminary objection in the form of a demurrer and dismissed the Petition for Review. The court held that a non-content based sales tax that did not single out particular speakers did not violate the free speech rights protected under the United States or Pennsylvania Constitutions.

Machipongo Land & Coal Co. v. Department of Envtl. Resources


NO. 248 M.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


155 Pa. Commw. 72; 624 A.2d 742; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 230


December 15, 1992, Argued  
April 15, 1993, Decided  
April 15, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied May 14, 1993.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding, petitioners, coal company and coal owners, sought equitable and declaratory relief against respondents, the Department of Environmental Resources (DER), the Environmental Quality Board, and the Secretary of Environmental Resources, after the DER designated petitioners' land unsuitable for surface mining pursuant to § 4.5(b) of the Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act, 52 P.S. § 1396.4e(b).


OVERVIEW: Respondent Environmental Quality Board (EQB) designated property owned by petitioners, coal company and coal owners, as unsuitable for surface mining pursuant to § 4.5(b) of the Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act (PaSMCRA), 52 P.S. § 1396.4e(b). Petitioners sought declaratory and injunctive relief against respondents, the Department of Environmental Resources, the EQB, and the Secretary of Environmental Resources, claiming that PaSMCRA constituted a taking without just compensation and that the EQB's designation was otherwise unlawful. The court denied petitioners' request for relief, first concluding that the EQB did not expire under the Sunset Act, 71 P.S. §§ 1795.1-1795.14, before it designated petitioners' property because the Sunset Act was unconstitutional. The court also found that PaSMCRA was not unconstitutional on its face and that the issue of whether a taking occurred under PaSMCRA could only be determined by examining the statute's effect on petitioners' property. Further, the court transferred the matter to the Environmental Hearing Board (EHB) under the doctrine of primary jurisdiction for further examination of the takings issue.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order denying petitioner coal company's and coal owners' request for declaratory and injunctive relief because the Environmental Quality Board did not expire under the Sunset Act before it designated petitioners' property as unsuitable for mining and the Surface Mining Conservation and Reclamation Act was not unconstitutional on its face. The court transferred the matter to the Environmental Hearing Board for further review.

Surgical Laser Technologies v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Revenue

OVERVIEW: The legislature enacted 72 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 7401(3)4., which allowed companies to carry forward their net operating losses and deduct them from income in succeeding years. The state publicized the availability of the carryforward as an incentive to businesses. Ten years later the legislature amended § 7401(3)4., eliminating the carryforward. Respondent filed preliminary objections. The court overruled the preliminary objections. OUTCOME: The court dismissed the preliminary objections of respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Revenue to the complaint in equity of petitioner corporation, because the allegations in the petition were sufficient to establish a possible due process violation or statutorily created non-uniformity.

 

645 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Harper v. State Employees' Retirement Sys.


NO. 360 M.D. 1990


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 573; 624 A.2d 279; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 215


December 18, 1991, Argued  
April 6, 1993, Decided  
April 6, 1993, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner legislators and respondent retirement system filed cross-motions for summary judgment in an action for declaratory judgment that amendments to the State Employees' Retirement Code of 1974, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5101 et seq., which eliminated a compensation option to receive better pension benefits for new legislators, denied petitioners equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Pa. Const. art. I, § 1 and Pa. Const. art. III, § 32.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner legislators were eligible for pension benefits that were less attractive than benefits for incumbent legislators because of changes made to the State Employees' Retirement Code of 1974, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5101 et seq., before petitioners took office. On cross-motions for summary judgment, the court upheld the law because there was no equal protection violation under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, Pa. Const. art. I, § 1, Pa. Const. art. III, § 32, or under existing case law. The legislation did not change existing contractual rights, the new legislators were not members of a suspect class, and the receipt of benefits did not implicate a liberty interest. The legislation was rational because it averted a pension fund shortfall. The court held that petitioners were not entitled to the same protection that the law afforded the judiciary from legislative interference. The court found that, unlike the situation where the legislature might use funding to control a separate branch of government, which could violate the separation of powers and Pa. Const. art. V, § 16(a), the pension problem arose from the legislature itself, not as a threat by another branch of government.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner legislators' motion for summary judgment and granted respondent retirement system's motion for summary judgment because there was no equal protection violation absent interference with an existing contact, a suspect class, or a fundamental liberty interest; and, provisions that dealt with the separation of powers did not apply because the legislature was dealing with its own compensation.

Pennsylvania Medical Soc'y v. Foster


No. 137 M.D. 1990


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 562; 624 A.2d 274; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 220


February 1, 1993, Argued  
April 6, 1993, Decided  
April 6, 1993, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff medical society filed an action to declare 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1797, a provision of the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law that restricted charges and billing for automobile accident medical treatment, unconstitutional as violative of physicians' due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art I, § 1, and because it was vague and overbroad. The court considered cross-motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff medical society challenged the constitutionality of 43 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1797, a provision of the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law that restricted charges to insurers of automobile accident victims to a percentage of the Medicare payments and also prohibited billing the patient any shortfall. The court granted respondent commissioner's motion for summary judgment. The court held that § 1797(a) did not violate physicians' due process rights under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Pa. Const. art I, § 1 because the state had a legitimate interest in regulating automobile insurance. In addition, § 1797(a) had a rational relationship to achieving that goal by restricting fees charged insurers, as well as preventing a shifting of the burden from the insurer to the insured for the shortfall. The court further held that respondent's interpretation of § 1797(a) was in accordance with the court's interpretation and was not clearly erroneous. The court also found that 31 Pa. Code § 69.22, a regulation adopted during the litigation, had eviscerated any contention regarding the purported unconstitutional vagueness of the direct patient billing prohibition.


OUTCOME: The court denied the summary judgment motion of plaintiff medical society, granted the cross-motion of respondent insurance commissioner, and dismissed the case. The court held that motor vehicle insurance regulation was a legitimate state interest, and the statute was rationally related to that interest and to the avoidance of cost shifting. The court held that respondent's regulations cured any vagueness deficiencies.

Rybak v. State Employees' Retirement Bd.


NO. 134 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 586; 624 A.2d 286; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 237


September 11, 1991, Argued  
April 6, 1993, Decided  
April 6, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Granted July 26, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Pa. LEXIS 173.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED From Order dated January 3, 1991. State Agency, State Employees' Retirement Board


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner legislator appealed the order of the State Agency, State Employees' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), which rejected his request to receive higher pension benefits. The board held that petitioner, who served as a legislator prior to amendments to the State Employees' Retirement Code of 1974, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5101, et seq., but was not in office at the time of the amendments, would receive reduced benefits for later terms.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner legislator had served, but was out of office and receiving pension benefits, when the legislature amended the state pension system under the State Employee's Retirement Code of 1974, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. 5101, et seq., to provide lower pension benefits to new legislators. Petitioner later took office again and served under the changed system. When he retired, he sought to be classified with legislators who had taken office under the old system. Respondent retirement board, while not disturbing his former pension rights, ordered that the pension for his later service be based on membership in the class of new legislators. On appeal, the court affirmed, and held that the two-tier system did not violate the equal protection provisions of U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Pa. Const. art. I, § 1 and Pa Const. art. III, § 32, because the system was rationally related to restoring fiscal soundness to the system. The court held that petitioner's vested contract rights had not been unconstitutionally impaired because the two separate segments of service, one before and one after the amendments, constituted two separate employment contracts and two separate sets of pension rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent retirement board that gave petitioner legislator a lower pension for later service after changes to the pension system because the two-tier retirement system for legislators did not deny petitioner equal protection under either the federal or state constitutions, and petitioner's two periods of employment involved two distinct employment contracts and two distinct sets of pension rights.

 

648 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Commonwealth v. Seigworth


NO. 2154 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 458; 624 A.2d 223; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 198


March 1, 1993, Argued  
March 31, 1993, Decided  
March 31, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal and/or Cross-Petition Denied November 17, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED From No. 876 - 1991 C.D. Common Pleas Court of Jefferson County. Judge WILLIAM HENRY, President Judge


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant farmer challenged an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Jefferson County (Pennsylvania), which denied his motion in arrest of judgment and upheld the guilty verdict against him for a violation of the Game and Wildlife Code.


OVERVIEW: Defendant farmer killed a deer that was destroying his crops and reported the killing as required by the Game and Wildlife Code. Defendant was cited by a wildlife control officer for unlawfully failing to care for the carcass under 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2125 and found guilty of failure or neglect to care for the carcass, or any part thereof, of any game or wildlife other than raccoons under 34 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2126(a)(5). On appeal, the court reversed, and found that it was required to strictly construe penal provisions by 1 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1928(b). The court found that the term "care for a carcass" was not defined, and there was no basis for linking failing to care under § 2126(a)(5) with the removal of entrails in § 2125 because there were no shared, parallel, or referenced terms between the sections, and there were indications that failure to care was something other than failure to remove entrails. The court, therefore, concluded that defendant's conviction was improper. The court, therefore, determined that it needed not reach defendant's constitutional challenge of § 2126(a)(5).


OUTCOME: Defendant farmer's conviction for violation of the Game and Wildlife Code was reversed by the court because under the required strict interpretation of statutory penal provisions, there was no reason to link failure to care with the removal of entrails of deer killed by defendant.

 

649 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Mock v. Department of Envtl. Resources


NO. 1153 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 380; 623 A.2d 940; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 186; 23 ELR 21290


November 18, 1992, Argued  
March 25, 1993, Decided  
March 25, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied December 20, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From EHB Docket No. 90-166-MR. State Agency, Environmental Hearing Board


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowners appealed a decision of the Pennsylvania Environmental Hearing Board, which upheld the denial of petitioners' permit to fill wetlands on their property to construct an auto repair shop, and which ruled that such denial was not an unconstitutional taking.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner landowners applied for a permit to fill wetlands on their property for the purpose of constructing an auto repair shop. The Pennsylvania Environmental Hearing Board upheld the denial of petitioners' permit. The court affirmed the decision, and held that there was no unconstitutional taking. The court found that petitioners did not prove that their land was valueless after the permit denial. The court held that although petitioners might have been prevented from the most profitable use of their property, reduction in value was not enough to find a taking. The court found that the Dam Safety and Encroachments Act, 32 P.S. § 693.1-.27, and the Department of Environmental Resources' regulations did not prohibit the filling of wetlands, nor did the permit denial prohibit all construction on petitioners' land. The court held that petitioners' reasonable investment-backed expectations were not frustrated to the point that effected a taking of their property. The court found that petitioners did not offer any evidence about the economic value of their land that could be realized through other development options.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the environmental hearing board's decision that the denial of petitioner landowners' permit to fill wetlands was not an unconstitutional taking. The court concluded that the board's finding that the land in its current state was valueless did not mean that petitioners' land had to remain undeveloped and devoid of value in the future despite the environmental regulations.

 

650 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Cooper v. State Bd. of Medicine


No. 1783 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 234; 623 A.2d 433; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 148


December 17, 1992, Argued  
March 12, 1993, Decided  
March 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied November 10, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED From No. 0530-49-91, File No. 90-49-01505. State Agency, Pennsylvania State Board of Medicine


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor sought review of a decision of the Pennsylvania State Board of Medicine, which denied his motion to dismiss or suspend disciplinary proceedings pending against him. Petitioner contended that respondent board could not prosecute and adjudicate his case, and that his due process rights were violated by a failure to provide information through discovery.


OVERVIEW: Respondent board authorized formal discipline action against petitioner doctor. It charged him with multiple counts of unprofessional conduct. Petitioner filed an answer to the complaint and a motion to dismiss in which he alleged that respondent could not be both the prosecutor and the adjudicator in his case. Respondent affirmed a hearing examiner decision to overrule that motion, then decided that a court should decide if it could adjudicate the case. The court granted permission for petitioner to appeal respondent's certified interlocutory order. The court concluded that respondent was not required to have a completely separate body render the final adjudication in the case, as long as respondent excluded, in the final stages of the proceedings, members who performed prosecutorial functions. The court also held that petitioner's due process rights were not violated by a letter that informed him that there was no formal discovery in an administrative proceeding, but that it would comply with most of petitioner's requests at a pre-hearing conference. The case was remanded to respondent for final adjudication in accordance with the opinion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent board that it could adjudicate in petitioner doctor's disciplinary proceedings because administrative boards had both investigatory and prosecutorial functions, but remanded the case with instruction that it be adjudicated by members who had not participated in petitioner's prosecution. The court held that petitioner doctor's due process rights were not violated by informal pre-hearing discovery.

 

651 of 892 DOCUMENTS


State's Employees' Retirement Bd. v. Pennsylvania Human Relations Comm'n


No. 946 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 55; 622 A.2d 412; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 121


December 16, 1992, Argued  
March 5, 1993, Decided  
March 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. E-35205A. State Agency, Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state retirement board challenged the judgment of respondent Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission, which ordered petitioner to cease discriminating against applicants for disability insurance based upon the applicants' age and declared void, as illegally discriminatory, 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5102.


OVERVIEW: Based on a complaint from an employee, respondent Pennsylvania Human Relations Commission ordered petitioner State Employees' Retirement Board to cease and desist discriminating based on age against employees who applied for disability insurance. Petitioner challenged respondent's order, and argued that it was required by 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5308, to refuse disability insurance to those who had reached superannuation age. The court reversed and vacated respondent's order. The court held that respondent had not been given the power to declare a statute invalid because that statute was discriminatory. The court held that 43 P.S. § 955 (Supp. 1977-8), which prohibited discrimination against employees, did not supercede the provisions of 71 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5308, with regard to the limitations on availability of disability insurance because § 5308 was passed at a later time and because it was the more specific statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and vacated respondent's order. The court held that respondent did not have the authority to declare a statute invalid, and that the statute which prohibited discrimination was a general statute and was passed before the more specific statute which limited the availability of disability insurance based on an employees age.

 

652 of 892 DOCUMENTS


Shultz v. Workmen's Compensation Appeal Bd. (Leroy Roofing Co. & PMA Group)


NO. 1288 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


154 Pa. Commw. 34; 621 A.2d 1239; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 118


October 23, 1992, Submitted  
March 3, 1993, Decided  
March 3, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied December 2, 1994, Reported at: 1994 Pa. LEXIS 714.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. A90-1178. State Agency, Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner widow appealed the decision of respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Pennsylvania), which affirmed a referee's decision to terminate death benefits to petitioner because petitioner had entered into a meretricious relationship with another man pursuant to 77 P.S. § 562.


OVERVIEW: Respondent employer filed a petition to discontinue the payment of death benefits to petitioner widow because she was living with another man. The referee granted the petition, and respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board (Board) affirmed. Petitioner appealed the Board's judgment, and argued that 77 P.S. § 562, which discontinued death benefits if the surviving spouse entered into a meretricious relationship with another, was unconstitutional because it violated her privacy, equal protection and due process rights and operated as a bill of attainder. The court affirmed the Board's decision. The court held that no suspect group was created by § 562 and no privacy interest was violated by that statute. The court held that the state had a rational basis for the statute, which was to encourage legally recognized relationships. The court held that the statute does not operate as a bill of attainder. The court held that the Board properly analyzed the economic impact to petitioner of discontinuing the death benefits.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed respondent Workmen's Compensation Appeal Board 's order to terminate death benefits because the workmen's compensation statute specifically called for the discontinuance of death benefits to persons who entered into meretricious relationships, the statute did not violate petitioner widow's equal protection, privacy or due process rights, and the statute did not operate as a bill of attainder.

Heinly v. Commonwealth


NO. 904 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


153 Pa. Commw. 599; 621 A.2d 1212; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 111


December 17, 1992, Argued  
February 26, 1993, Decided  
February 26, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. 1991-C-9044. Common Pleas Court of Northampton County. Judge ROBERT E. SIMPSON, JR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant shooting victim challenged an order of the Common Pleas Court of Northampton County (Pennsylvania), which sustained a demurrer filed by appellees, state, police commissioner, and police officers, and dismissed appellant's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 civil rights complaint. Appellees claimed sovereign immunity and asserted that appellant had failed to state any cause of action on which relief could be granted.


OVERVIEW: Appellant shooting victim was injured during a stand-off between his brother and the police; appellant filed a personal injury suit which alleged reckless misconduct, intentional failure to properly train the police and protect bystanders, and violation of his civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellees, state, police commissioner, and police officers, filed a demurrer which asserted sovereign immunity and failure to state a cause of action, which was granted and resulted in the dismissal of appellant's suit. On appeal, the court affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded the cause. It held that the Pennsylvania Sovereign Immunity Act, 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8522(b), did not immunize appellee police officers from a 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action, and appellant's complaint was sufficient to implicate federal rights guaranteed under U.S. Const. amends. IV, XIV. The ruling as to appellee police officers was reversed and remanded. The court affirmed the ruling as to the remaining appellees, holding that the state was immune from suit and that appellant failed to plead that defendant supervising officers did not adequately train and supervise other officers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded the cause. The court reversed and remanded as to appellee police officers because they were not immune from liability arising out of for their individual actions under federal civil rights law. The court affirmed as to the remaining appellees, as the state was immune and appellant failed to state a legally sustainable claim against appellee supervising officers.

North Cambria Fuel Co. v. Commonwealth Dep't of Envtl. Resources


NO. 896 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


153 Pa. Commw. 489; 621 A.2d 1155; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 88


October 22, 1992, Argued  
February 12, 1993, Decided  
February 12, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal and/or Cross-Petition Granted February 24, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. EHB Docket No. 85-297-G. State Agency, Environmental Hearing Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner fuel company sought review of the order of the Pennsylvania Environmental Hearing Board, which affirmed two compliance orders issued by respondent, the Department of Environmental Resources, which required abatement of discharges from petitioner's surface mine site, regardless of whether petitioner was responsible for generating the discharges.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner fuel company operated a surface mine and was ordered to abate discharges from its mine site by respondent, the Department of Environmental Resources. Petitioner challenged the orders because it claimed it was an adjacent mining operation which was responsible for the discharges from petitioner's site due to fugitive water and the Environmental Hearing Board affirmed the orders. On appeal, the court affirmed the board's action because the Clean Streams Law (CSL), 35 P.S. § 691.315(a) imposed liability on petitioner because the discharges emanated from its property and neither causation nor fault was required to establish that liability. The court found that liability under the CSL was not founded in tort and, thus, no causal link was necessary for liability to attach; CSL liability was based upon the police power of the commonwealth and was reasonably exercised thereunder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the compliance orders issued by respondent, the Department of Environmental Resources, to petitioner fuel company requiring that petitioner abate the discharge of acid mine drainage from its surface mining site because causation and fault were not required for liability to attach for the discharges.

In re Appeal of Sidorek


No. 1016 C. D. 1992, No. 1094 C. D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


153 Pa. Commw. 476; 621 A.2d 1149; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 89


December 15, 1992, Argued  
February 12, 1993, Decided  
February 12, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. 1127 Civil 1991. Common Pleas Court of Susquehanna County. Judge KENNETH W. SEAMANS


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of Susquehanna County (Pennsylvania), which remanded appellee taxpayers' tax assessment appeal to appellant's Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes to give appellees the same tax treatment as their neighbors with similar adjoining land. Appellant claimed it had established a different treatment based on adjoining land owner farmed on the land.


OVERVIEW: Appellee taxpayers appealed a tax assessment to the trial court after appellant county's Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes determined that appellees should pay a property tax at a rate different from an adjacent landowner, who was farming the land, when appellees was not farming. Appellant sought reversal of the trial court order and claimed appellant had established a different tax treatment for landowners who farmed their land from those that did not pursuant to the authority of the Pennsylvania Farmland and Forest Land Assessment Act of 1974 (Farmland Act), 72 P.S. §§ 5490.1-5490.13 (1974). The court affirmed the trial court's order and held appellant had violated Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1, as a matter of law by setting different tax rates for landowners depending on whether the land was actively farmed or not, when the properties were similar in character and adjacent to each other, and the Farmland Act did not authorize appellant to establish the disparate rates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order remanding appellee taxpayers property tax assessment back to appellant county's Board of Assessment and Revision of Taxes, because appellant was not authorized to establish a different rate for appellees based on appellees not actively farming on the land and such a disparate rate was unconstitutional.

Equitable Life Assurance Soc'y v. Murphy


No. 763 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


153 Pa. Commw. 338; 621 A.2d 1078; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 74


June 18, 1992, Argued  
February 5, 1993, Decided  
February 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. 4446 January Term, 1987. Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia County. Judge BERNARD J. GOODHEART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, an insurance company and real estate corporation, sought review of the judgment of the Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia (Pennsylvania), which granted summary judgment to appellees, the city and its revenue commissioner, for payment of delinquent realty transfer taxes, because appellants claimed the Philadelphia Realty Transfer Tax Ordinance was invalid and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, an insurance company and real estate corporation, failed to file a certificate of transfer on a real estate transaction which occurred outside the city of Philadelphia as required by the Bill No. 567 amendment to Phila., Pa., Code § 19-1403 and claimed that the imposition of such a tax violated the Sterling Act, 53 P.S. § 15971 and was unconstitutional on its face and as applied to appellants. Appellees, the city and its revenue commissioner, sought payment of the delinquent transfer tax and, on appeal, the court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees. The transfer of stock of a real estate corporation constituted a transfer of the interests in the property held by the corporation and was, therefore, properly taxed by appellees. The court held that Bill No. 567 did not classify the subjects of taxation uniformly as required by Pa. Const. art. VIII, § 1, or U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1, but that the offending "more than one percent" provision could be severed without subverting or ignoring the express intent of the city council to tax all such realty transfers. The imposition of a transfer tax on real estate corporations was held constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellees, the city and its revenue commissioner, because appellants, an insurance company and real estate corporation, were proper subjects for realty transfer taxation because the city ordinance was constitutionally applied to transfers of city real estate even where actual transfer occurred elsewhere.

Dowler v. Public School Employee's Retirement Bd.


NO. 751 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


153 Pa. Commw. 109; 620 A.2d 639; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 45


November 19, 1992, Argued  
January 27, 1993, Decided  
January 27, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From File No. 236-20-8089/Dowler. State Agency, Public School Employes' Retirement Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant appealed an order of respondent Public School Employees' Retirement Board (Pennsylvania), which rejected the proposed report of a hearing examiner who suggested ruling in favor of claimant on appeal from a decision of the Pennsylvania State Employee's Retirement System, which refused to consider a payment of $ 14,854.08 made to claimant as compensation for retirement purposes.


OVERVIEW: In anticipation of his retirement, petitioner claimant entered into an agreement with his employing school district that allowed him to work a reduced schedule for full-time pay. In addition, the school district agreed to pay petitioner $ 14,854.08 to purchase retirement credit for his military service, which the retirement system concluded was a severance payment and excluded in calculating petitioner's final average salary. He appealed, arguing that circumstances did not allow him to receive the benefit of the agreement, and hence the school district characterized the payment as compensation for his after-hour negotiation work in addition to full-time service as personnel director. Respondent Public School Employees' Retirement Board rejected its hearing examiner's recommendation to include the payment in calculating petitioner's final average salary, and concluded that the money was a severance payment. The court affirmed, holding that even if petitioner was not paid pursuant to the written agreement, the payment made was not part of his regular salary. The court held that respondent correctly found it was severance payment, and in doing so, did not deny petitioner due process.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of respondent Public School Employees' Retirement Board, holding that its review of the record indicated that respondent did not deprive petitioner of procedural due process. The court affirmed the board's order, finding that there was substantial evidence in the record to support the board's findings, which supported the conclusion of law that the claimant received a severance payment in the amount of $ 14,854.08.

Transcontinental Gas Pipe Line Corp. v. Commonwealth


No. 35 F.R. 1989, No. 37 F.R. 1989

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner interstate seller of gas appealed orders of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which imposed a utilities gross receipts tax on petitioner, plus a penalty and interest.


OVERVIEW: A utilities gross receipts tax was imposed on petitioner interstate seller of gas, plus penalty and interest, and petitioner appealed. The court held that petitioner was not exempt from the tax because all of petitioner's sales were not for resale. The court held that the tax did not violate the commerce clause because the tax was internally and externally consistent, did not discriminate against interstate commerce, and was related to the services provided. The court held that tax liability was to be applied to petitioner only prospectively from the date it was put on notice of the possibility that it was not exempt from the tax. The orders were affirmed as modified to apply only to prospective enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the orders imposing a utilities gross receipts tax plus penalty and interest on petitioner interstate seller of gas, as modified to apply only to prospective enforcement, holding that petitioner was not exempt from the tax, and that the tax did not violate the commerce clause, state uniformity clause, or equal protection clause.

Bunch v. State Bd. of Auctioneer Examiners


No. 351 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


152 Pa. Commw. 616; 620 A.2d 578; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 22; 1993-1 Trade Cas. (CCH) P70,095


November 19, 1992, Argued  
January 14, 1993, Decided  
January 14, 1993, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied March 11, 1993, Reported at 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 169. Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied March 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED From No. 88-64-01369. State Agency, State Board of Auctioneer Examiners



DISPOSITION: In view of such constitutional infirmities, which the Supreme Court also found in Lyness, we reverse the Board's order and remand to the Board with instructions to devise a non-commingled approach to Bunch's appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner auctioneer sought review of an order from respondent State Board of Auctioneer Examiners (Pennsylvania), which revoked petitioner's license to practice as an auctioneer.


OVERVIEW: Respondent state board of auctioneer examiners entered an order that revoked petitioner auctioneer's license to practice as an auctioneer. Petitioner had pleaded guilty to bid pooling in violation of 15 U.S.C.S. § 1 of the Sherman Antitrust Act. Respondent found that 63 P.S. § 734.26(a) of the Auctioneer and Auction Licensing Act (Act) required revocation of petitioner's license. On appeal, the court found that respondent was required to either revoke or suspend petitioner's license under § 734.26(a) of the Act when it determined that bid pooling was a like offense, and that petitioner's conviction occurred during the term of his licensure as an auctioneer. However, the court held that respondent's order was unconstitutional because 63 P.S. § 734.20(a) of the Act improperly allowed the commingling of the prosecutorial and adjudicatory roles of respondent. The court reversed respondent's order and remanded with instructions to devise a non-commingled approach to petitioner's appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed respondent state board of auctioneer examiners' order, which revoked petitioner auctioneer's license to practice as an auctioneer, because respondent's fact-finding function did not authorize it to prosecute petitioner.

Krug v. City of Philadelphia


No. 2164 C. D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


152 Pa. Commw. 475; 620 A.2d 46; 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 1


November 16, 1992, Argued  
January 5, 1993, Decided  
January 5, 1993, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. 2267 January Term, 1989. Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia County. Judge RUSSELL M. NIGRO


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought a review of an order of the Common Pleas Court of Philadelphia County (Pennsylvania), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and directed appellant to pay delinquent wage and net profit taxes as well as fines.


OVERVIEW: After appellant taxpayer failed to pay the wage and net profit taxes imposed against him by appellee city, in a suit to collect, the lower court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment and directed appellant to pay the delinquent wage and net profit taxes as well as fines. On appeal, the court affirmed the order of the lower court holding that under Philadelphia, Pa., Code § 19-1701, appellant was required to appeal the imposition of the taxes to the tax review board (board), which appellant failed to do. The court further held that pursuant to 2 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 752, and 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 933, before appellant could have appealed to the lower court, he was required to have exhausted his remedies with the board. Finally, the court held that because appellant had failed to exhaust his administrative remedies, he had waived, on appeal to the court, his defenses to the imposition of the taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order of the lower court, which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and directed appellant taxpayer to pay delinquent wage and net profit taxes as well as fines. Appellant waived his defenses to the taxes because he failed to appeal to the tax review board.

Teamsters Local 115 v. Pennsylvania Labor Relations Bd.


No. 1676 C.D. 1991, No. 1736 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


152 Pa. Commw. 394; 619 A.2d 382; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 776


March 4, 1992, Argued  
December 29, 1992, Decided  
December 29, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Application for Reargument Denied February 23, 1993, Reported at 1993 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 108.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEALED From Nos. PERA-C-91-195-E and PERA-C-91-230-E. State Agency, Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, the orders of the Board dismissing the Unions exceptions and unfair labor practices charges are reversed, and the Board is ordered to entertain the charges in order to determine whether complaints should be issued against the Employer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union challenged the orders of respondent Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, which dismissed petitioner's exceptions to respondent's decision that it lacked jurisdiction over unfair labor practice charges filed by petitioner against an employer, the Court of Common Pleas of Philadelphia County. Respondent brought claims under the Public Employe Relations Act, Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, §§ 1101.101 to 1101.2301.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner union filed unfair labor practices charges pursuant to the Public Employe Relations Act (Act 195), Pa. Stat. Ann. tit. 43, §§ 1101.101 to 1101.2301, against the employer, the Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County, after certain positions with that court were reclassified and privatized. Respondent Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board declined jurisdiction pursuant to the doctrine of separation of powers and dismissed the charges. Petitioner appealed, and the court reversed. Initially, the court concluded that it had jurisdiction to hear the appeal under 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 763. On the merits, the court concluded that the employees must be given a forum in which to vindicate their rights and that respondent's assumption of jurisdiction did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers. Respondent was the only forum which entertained unfair labor practices charges, and failing to accept jurisdiction would eliminate the employees' rights under Act 195. Also, Pa. Const. art. I, § 11, provided that a remedy must exist for every right. Providing the employees with the right to organize was illusory without the corresponding right to a forum in which they could be heard.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of respondent Pennsylvania Labor Relations Board, which dismissed petitioner union's exceptions and unfair labor practices charges. The court ordered respondent to determine whether complaints should be issued against the employer, Court of Common Pleas, Philadelphia County. The court concluded that respondent's assumption of jurisdiction did not violate the doctrine of separation of powers.

Amoroso v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp., Bureau of Driver Licensing


No. 2272 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

December 11, 1992, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from an order entered by the Court of Common Pleas of Adams County (Pennsylvania), which denied an appeal from the suspension of his motor vehicle operating privilege by the state driver's license bureau as a consequence of defendant's convictions for violating 35 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 780-113(a)(30).

Stat. § 13(a)(30), his driving privilege was suspended for periods of 90 days, and one and two years. The court affirmed the decision, finding defendant's constitutional attack on the mandatory penalty provisions of § 13(m) constituted a collateral attack of the criminal proceedings to which he pled guilty and was, therefore, beyond the court's limited scope of review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's suspension of defendant's operating privileges because defendant's constitutional attack on the mandatory penalty provision constituted a collateral attack of the criminal proceedings to which he pled guilty and was, therefore, beyond the court's limited scope of review.

Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp., Bureau of Driver Licensing v. Malizio


NO. 611 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


152 Pa. Commw. 57; 618 A.2d 1091; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 722


October 9, 1992, Submitted on Briefs  
December 2, 1992, Decided  
December 2, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. S.A. 2785 of 1991. Common Pleas Court of Allegheny County. Judge RAYMOND L. SCHEIB



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, DOT met all the requirements to suspend Malizio's license under § 1547 of the Vehicle Code, and the order of the trial court must be reversed and the license suspension reinstated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Transportation challenged the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which sustained the appeal of appellee driver from a 12-month driver's license suspension for refusal to submit to a chemical test under the implied consent law of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547.


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver was stopped by a police officer, and asked to perform a series of field sobriety tests which he failed. The officer then asked appellee to submit to chemical testing, but he refused. Thereafter, appellant Department of Transportation ordered a 12-month suspension of appellee's driver's license for refusal to submit to a chemical test under the implied consent law of the Vehicle Code, 75 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1547. Appellant sought review of the trial court's judgment sustaining appellee's challenge of the suspension, and the court reversed. The court held that the trial court erred in requiring the police to prove probable cause for the traffic stop because the license suspension matter was a civil proceeding in which the probable cause standard was inapplicable. The court found that the proper standard of review was whether appellant had met its burden of proof. As appellee's testimony and the trial court's findings of fact were sufficient to establish reasonable grounds for the officer to believe that appellee was operating his vehicle under the influence of alcohol, the court ruled that appellant met all the requirements for suspension under § 1547.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee driver, and reinstated the 12-month suspension of his driver's license. The court held that appellant Department of Transportation met all the statutory requirements to suspend the license, and the trial court erred in requiring a probable cause showing as that standard was not applicable to a civil suspension proceeding.

WANDER v. FOSTER


No. 2692 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


152 Pa. Commw. 23; 618 A.2d 1077; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 717


October 20, 1992, Argued  
December 1, 1992, Decided  
December 1, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From Docket No. A91-04-16. State Agency, Insurance Commissioner


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner citizen sought review of a decision from respondent Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania), which affirmed the denial of petitioner's application for a bail bondsman's license.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's application for a bail bondsmen license was denied because of a prior felony conviction and objections to his application by a county district attorney. Respondent Insurance Commissioner affirmed the denial of petitioner's license because petitioner made threats against the county district attorney who opposed his application. On review, the court affirmed respondent's decision. The court found that 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5743, which governed bail bondsmen's licenses, was not unconstitutionally vague when read with 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 5746(b), which provided grounds for suspension and revocation of a license, and that the statutes together gave respondent the criteria and standards for either approving or denying a bail bondsmen's license. The court held that the discretion to grant or refuse license applications was in the discretion of respondent and that the court's review was limited only to a showing of abuse of discretion or arbitrary exercise of authority. The court affirmed the finding that petitioner's threats established that he was not sufficiently rehabilitated from his prior felony conviction to warrant approval of a bail bondsmen's license.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of respondent Insurance Commissioner. The court held that the record established that respondent did not abuse her discretion when she denied petitioner's application for a bondsmen license because petitioner made certain threats made in an attempt to force withdrawal of opposition to his application.

Magazine Publishers of Am. v. Department of Revenue


NO. 74 M.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


151 Pa. Commw. 592; 618 A.2d 1056; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 711; 21 Media L. Rep. 1215


September 14, 1992, Argued  
November 25, 1992, Decided  
November 25, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Reargument Denied December 18, 1992, Reported at: 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 757.



DISPOSITION: Petitioners' application for summary relief is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a trade association and several publishing companies, filed a motion for summary judgment in their action against respondent Department of Revenue that sought an order declaring the state's general sales and use tax to be unconstitutional as applied to magazines and enjoining respondent from collecting the tax.


OVERVIEW: Section 7204 of the Tax Reform Code of 1971, 72 P.S. § 7204, was amended, and the magazine exclusion from the sales tax provision was deleted. Petitioners, a trade association and several publishing companies, filed a complaint for declaratory and injunctive relief against respondent Department of Revenue alleging that the amendment violated their state and federal constitutional rights and seeking to enjoin respondent from collecting the tax. Petitioners filed for summary judgment relief, and the court denied their motion. The court held that the sales tax was not an attempt to discriminate on the basis of the content of the taxpayer's speech, single out magazines for special treatment, or impede the free flow of ideas. As the sales tax focused on the format and frequency of the publication without regard to content, the court ruled that the amendment did not violate petitioners' U.S. Const. amend. I rights. The court concluded that there was a reasonable basis for the distinction in the law between newspapers and magazines, and, therefore, the tax also did not violate petitioners' rights under the equal protection or uniformity clauses.


OUTCOME: The court denied the summary judgment relief requested by petitioners, a trade association and several publishing companies. The court held that the challenged sales tax was not an attempt to discriminate on the basis of the content of the taxpayer's speech, single out magazines for special treatment, or impede the free flow of ideas.

Boyle v. Commonwealth, Dep't of Transp.


NO. 160 M.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


151 Pa. Commw. 430; 617 A.2d 70; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 684


July 17, 1992, Submitted on Briefs  
November 12, 1992, Decided  
November 12, 1992, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner injured person filed a civil action for damages against respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania Department of Transportation in the Court of Common Pleas of Lackawanna County (Pennsylvania), which arose out of an automobile accident. Respondent's pleading asserted the affirmative defense of immunity under 1 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2310, and petitioner filed for a declaratory judgment to determine the immunity issue.


OVERVIEW: In an tort action against respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania Department of Transportation, petitioner injured person filed a declaratory action which sought a declaration that 1 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 2310, on sovereign immunity, and 42 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 8528, on the limitation of damages, were violative of and offensive to his rights under the U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. III § 32. Petitioner alleged that these statutes denied him interests, liberties, rights, and benefits that were enjoyed by victims of private tortfeasors by precluding recovery of damages in an amount commensurate with his loss. The court dismissed the petition. The court noted that it could refuse to render or enter a declaratory judgment where such judgment, if rendered or entered, would not terminate the uncertainty or controversy giving rise to the proceeding and that declaratory relief was not available unless an actual controversy existed or was imminent. The court determined that petitioner's declaratory action was not ripe because the controversy would only have existed if a jury found respondent liable and returned a verdict against them that exceeded the statutory limitation on damages.


OUTCOME: The court on review sustained respondent Commonwealth of Pennsylvania, Department of Transportation's preliminary objections and dismissed petitioner injured person's declaratory judgment action. The court held that declaratory relief was not available unless an actual controversy existed and that a controversy would not exist unless and if a jury returned a verdict for petitioner which exceeded the statutory limitation on damages.

Giffin v. Chronister


NO. 213 M.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


151 Pa. Commw. 286; 616 A.2d 1070; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 655


September 14, 1992, Argued  
October 26, 1992, Decided  
October 26, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. P91-10-35. State Agency, Insurance Commissioner of Commonwealth of Pennsylvania



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we will dismiss the preliminary objections and direct that the insurance commissioner plead to the complaint.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent insurance commissioner served petitioner insurance agent with an order to show cause to appear at a formal administrative hearing, and to show cause why respondent should not have imposed upon petitioner, penalties and loss of license. Petitioner then filed a complaint against respondent. Respondent filed preliminary objections to the complaint in the nature of a demurrer and an objection to the court's jurisdiction.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner insurance agent filed a complaint that requested that respondent insurance commissioner be enjoined from bringing proceedings for alleged violations of the Insurance Department Act, 40 P.S. §§ 1-321 and the Unfair Insurance Practices Act, 40 P.S. §§ 1171.1-1171.15. Respondent filed preliminary objections to the complaint in the nature of a demurrer and an objection to the court's jurisdiction. The court dismissed the preliminary objections and directed that respondent plead to the complaint. The court found that the complaint had asserted that the statutory framework of the Insurance Department created a system whereby respondent was both prosecutor and adjudicator in violation of due process rights. The court dismissed the preliminary objection in the nature of a demurrer because it was not clear from the face of the complaint that the law would not have permitted recovery. The court held that it had had jurisdiction, because the exhaustion of administrative remedies was not required due to the fact that the complaint had alleged that the statutory and regulatory framework as a whole commingled the prosecutorial and adjudicatory functions unconstitutionally.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the preliminary objections and directed that respondent insurance commissioner plead to petitioner insurance agent's complaint, because it was not clear that the law would not have permitted recovery, and because the court had jurisdiction over the complaint due to its constitutional attacks that had exempted petitioner from exhausting administrative procedures.

Stone & Edwards Ins. Agency v. Department of Ins.

Cons. Stat. § 102(a), as implemented by certain of respondent's regulations, created an unconstitutional commingling of the prosecutorial and adjudicative functions. The court dismissed respondent's objections and ordered that respondent plead to the complaint.

The demurrer was dismissed as it was unclear that the law would not permit recovery, and the court had jurisdiction as it was alleged that the entire statutory framework was unconstitutional.

In re Bear Creek Vill.


NO. 2628 C.D. 1991

OVERVIEW: Residents of a subdivision in appellant township filed a petition for incorporation as a borough pursuant to The Borough Code, 53 P.S. §§45101-48501. Appellant challenged the trial court's adoption of the findings the Borough Advisory Committee recommending approval of the petition. While the appeal was still pending the trial court issued an order certifying the question of incorporation for a referendum vote. After certifying the results of the vote, the trial court entered a final decree granting the petition for incorporation and appellant sought review of the decision. CASE SUMMARY:

Intervenors made a motion to quash the appeal.


OVERVIEW: After insurance department and automobile association had approved a settlement agreement which allowed automobile association to continue selling insurance in Pennsylvania, petitioner insurance agents' association filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that the agreement was contrary to law. No. 1934 C.D. 1991, No. 1935 C.D. 1991, No. 1972 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA

September 11, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal and/or Cross-Petition Granted March 4, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. G.D. 87-00166. Common Pleas Court of Allegheny County. Judge JAMES H. McLEAN



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County dated June 20, 1991 denying the parties' motions for post-trial relief, is hereby reversed and the case is remanded for entry of judgment n.o.v. Jurisdiction relinquished.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant family and borough challenged the decision of the Court of Common Pleas of Allegheny County (Pennsylvania), which denied their motions for a judgement non obstante veredicto and a new trial. The trial court awarded appellee neighbor damages on his civil rights claim that appellants violated his equal protection rights by conspiring to harass him and by denying him the same level of police services provided to appellant family.


OVERVIEW: On numerous occasions, appellant family and appellee neighbor had altercations that at times resulted in appellant family, who were members of the local fire department and council, calling the police and filing criminal charges against appellee. Appellee was never found guilty of the charges and filed, among other claims, a civil rights claim, under 42 U.S.C.S § 1983, against appellant family and the borough. Appellants challenged the trial court's decision after it entered judgment for appellee on the § 1983 claim and denied appellants' motions for a judgment non obstante veredicto (j.n.o.v.) and for a new trial. The court reversed the trial court's decision and held that appellants were entitled to j.n.o.v. because appellee failed to prove that appellant family acted under color of law, by using their public offices, to deprive appellee of his rights or that they conspired with the police to deprive him of his civil rights or the equal protection of the police. The court also found that appellee failed to establish appellant borough's liability under § 1983 because he failed to show that there was an official policy or custom that deprived him of his civil rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision, denying appellant family and borough's motion for a judgment non obstante veredicto, because the court found that appellee neighbor failed to show that appellant family used their official positions to deprive appellee his civil rights, that there was a conspiracy with the police to deny him equal protection, or that appellant borough had an official policy or custom that deprived him of his rights.

Reimer v. Board of Supervisors


NO. 2511 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


150 Pa. Commw. 323; 615 A.2d 938; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 581


June 16, 1992, Argued  
September 2, 1992, Decided  
September 2, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. 2910-C-1991. Common Pleas Court of Northampton County. Judge ROBERT E. SIMPSON, JR.



DISPOSITION: Like the Supreme Court in Middletown Township, we conclude that section 3.106 of the ordinance here is not in direct or inherent conflict with either The Clean Streams Law or the SFA. Accordingly, we affirm the order of the Court of Common Pleas of Northampton County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner filed a validity challenge to township's zoning ordinance with appellee board of superiors. The board rejected the challenge, and the Court of Common Pleas, Northampton County (Pennsylvania), affirmed the board's decision without taking further evidence. Appellant sought review.


OVERVIEW: Appellant landowner sought to subdivide a 15-acre tract into six lots. Appellee board of supervisors rejected the plan, based on a zoning ordinance which allowed only three lots on the tract. Appellant filed an action challenging the validity of the ordinance; the board rejected appellant's suit, and the trial court affirmed. Appellant sought review. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court, holding that the zoning ordinance constituted a legitimate exercise of the township's police power, that the large minimum lot sizes were justified as reasonably related to a legitimate public interest, and that the ordinance was tailored to burden only lots with certain issues. The ordinance did not violate uniformity requirements, because appellant's land had hazardous geological or topographical conditions, an exception to the requirements. The court held that the ordinance was not preempted by the Sewage Facilities Act, 35 P.S. §§ 750.1-750.20a, or in conflict with the Clean Streams Law, 35 P.S. §§ 691.1-691.1001.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, holding that the zoning ordinance constituted a legitimate exercise of the township's police power, that the large minimum lot sizes were justified as reasonably related to a legitimate public interest, and that the ordinance was tailored to burden only lots with certain issues. The ordinance did not violate uniformity requirements, because appellant's land had hazardous geological conditions.

Kalodner v. Commonwealth


No. 206 F.R. 1989


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


150 Pa. Commw. 248; 615 A.2d 900; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 570


June 19, 1992, Argued  
August 27, 1992, Decided  
August 27, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. RPIT-6547. State Agency, Board of Finance and Revenue



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, judgment is entered in favor of the Commonwealth.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant self-employeds challenged the order of the Board of Finance and Revenue (Pennsylvania), which disallowed deductions from their state individual income tax return for contributions made to their retirement plan.


OVERVIEW: Appellant self-employeds challenged the order of the state board of finance and revenue disallowing deductions from their individual income tax return for contributions to their retirement plans. Appellants argued that the department of revenue misinterpreted the tax code when it promulgated a regulation that denied self-employed individuals an exclusion from income for contributions to a qualified retirement plan, but granted employees an exclusion for employer contributions. The court disagreed holding that the department's interpretation was reasonable in that contributions by self-employed persons were not ordinary business expenses and therefore could not be deducted from net profits. The court also rejected appellant's argument that the regulation violated the federal equal protection rights and the uniformity clause of the state constitution because the court maintained there was a rational basis for distinction between self-employeds who invested income already received in a retirement plan, and situations where an employee's retirement fund was entirely funded by employer contributions. Accordingly the order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed because the court held that contributions by a self-employed person were not ordinary business expenses and therefore not deductible from net profits. The court also maintained that there was a rational basis for distinction between self-employeds who invested income already received in a retirement plan, and situations where a retirement fund was entirely funded by employer contributions.

Popowsky v. Pennsylvania Pub. Util. Comm'n


NO. 113 C.D. 1991, NO. 144 C.D. 1991


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


150 Pa. Commw. 166; 615 A.2d 857; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 561


December 18, 1991, Argued  
August 21, 1992, Decided  
August 21, 1992, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. R-901652. State Agency, Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission



DISPOSITION: Accordingly, we affirm the holding of the Commission Decision that Section 1327(e) of the Code applies to acquisitions of property by water and sewer utilities after the effective date of its enactment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners sought review of the order of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission, which rejected a request for an increase in rates for provision of water to consumers.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners sought an increase in rates charged to consumers for the provision of water. After the Pennsylvania Public Service Commission (PUC) rejected the request, petitioners appealed. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court reversed the finding that petitioners were not entitled to an expense item for an increase in income taxes due to a change in federal tax law repealing the option of deducting certain bad debts from taxable income. Under 26 U.S.C.S. § 166, taxpayers were permitted to amortize certain income over a period of four years, so there was no basis for denying the related bad debt expense item. The court affirmed, however, to the extent that it agreed with the lower court that 66 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1327(e), which applied to acquisitions of property by water and sewer utilities for a cost lower than depreciated original cost, applied after the effective date of enactment. Based on statutory construction, the statute was accorded prospective application. Although the statute could apply to conditions in place prior to enactment, that did not result in retroactive ratemaking, as a utility had no vested right to particular ratemaking formulas.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the decision of the Pennsylvania Public Utility Commission (PUC) in response to petitioners' effort to increase water rates. The court reversed denial of an expense item for a bad debt, while it affirmed the prospective application of a law pertaining to acquisition of property that affecting operating expenses. The case was remanded to the PUC for entry of a new order.

County of Bucks v. Cogan


No. 14 C.D. 1992


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


150 Pa. Commw. 74; 615 A.2d 810; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 550


June 19, 1992, Argued  
August 18, 1992, Decided  
August 18, 1992, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Allowance of Appeal Denied May 18, 1993.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEALED From No. 91-05716-09-1. Common Pleas Court of Bucks County. Judge WILLIAM HART RUFE, III



DISPOSITION: For the foregoing reasons the order of the trial court is vacated and this case is remanded for the trial court to conduct a hearing and make findings, and enter an order determining what bond is "good and sufficient" for Cogan.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax collector sought review of an order of the Court of Common Pleas of Bucks County (Pennsylvania), which denied her petition to allow her appeal from a certification of liability without an appeal bond or, alternatively, to reduce the amount of her appeal bond. Appellee liable party had filed a bond, and appellant had maintained that she lacked financial resources to purchase a bond.


OVERVIEW: Appellee County of Bucks (Pennsylvania) filed a certification of liability, under § 41 of the Local Tax Collection Law, against appellant tax collector and appellee liable party for taxes due. Appellant and appellee liable party sought review, and the trial court ordered that each post bond to the full liability amount. Appellant asked to be excused from posting bond or, alternatively, that her bond be reduced, as her financial resources prevented her from purchasing a bond. The trial court denied her request. Appellant argued that the bond requirements violated her due process rights and that two bonds were not required for the same certification of liability, under § 41(c) of the Local Tax Collection Law, 72 P.S. § 5511.41(c). The court vacated the order, holding that the trial court erroneously interpreted § 5511.41(c) to require a bond equal to the liability, as discretion was required, under § 5511.41(c). The case was remanded for a hearing on what a "good and sufficient" bond would be for appellant. The court opined that § 5511.41(c) did not excuse appellant from posting bond, as it required each party who appealed to post bond in order to discourage frivolous appeals.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order, holding that the trial court erred in determining that appellant tax collector was required to post an appeal bond equal to the amount of the certificate of liability because the Local Tax Collection Law required that the trial court use its discretion in setting the bond amount. The case was remanded for a determination of a "good and sufficient" bond for appellant.

Pennsylvania Medical Providers Ass'n v. Foster


No. 66 M. D. 1990


COMMONWEALTH COURT OF PENNSYLVANIA


149 Pa. Commw. 203; 613 A.2d 51; 1992 Pa. Commw. LEXIS 476


November 21, 1991, Argued  
July 10, 1992, Decided  
July 10, 1992, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Accordingly, the Commissioner's motion for summary judgment is granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania) filed a motion for summary judgment in an original jurisdiction action filed by petitioner medical providers association, which alleged that 74 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1797 of the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law was unconstitutional because it was vague and violated the due process clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. I, § 1.


OVERVIEW: 74 Pa. Cons. Stat. § 1797 of the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law established that medical treatment providers could not receive payment for treatment in excess of 110 percent of what Medicare would pay and that insurers must contract with peer review organizations to conform treatments to what was medically necessary. Petitioner medical providers association filed a petition for review in the court's original jurisdiction, alleging that § 1797 was unconstitutionally vague and violated the due process clauses of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Pa. Const. art. I, § 1. Respondent Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania) filed a motion for summary judgment. The court granted the motion for summary judgment in part, holding that § 1797 was not constitutionally vague, as 31 Pa. Code § 69.22 cured the vagueness; it required an insurer to notify a provider if an insured's first party benefits had been exhausted and § 1797 relied on the federal Medicare statute, which set forth peer review standards. Section 1797 did not violate due process, as 31 Pa. Code § 69.52(m) provided for judicial review of a peer review organization's final determination.


OUTCOME: The court granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Insurance Commissioner (Pennsylvania), holding that the Motor Vehicle Financial Responsibility Law was not constitutionally vague, as regulations required insurers to notify petitioner medical providers association if an insured's first party medical benefits had been exhausted. The Law did not violate due process, as regulations provided for judicial review.
